# Conversation Summary

## 1. Previous Conversation

The user tasked me with building **SpecBaker** - a CLI tool that transforms vague software goals into structured, implementation-ready specifications using IBM watsonx.ai. I successfully implemented the complete system according to the detailed implementation plan, including:

- Project foundation (package.json, CLI framework, configuration)
- Core modules (Goal Analyzer, Question Generator, Interactive Prompter, Context Builder, Spec Engine, Markdown Formatter)
- watsonx.ai integration
- All 11 specification sections
- CLI commands (generate, config, validate)
- Documentation and examples

## 2. Current Work

After initial implementation, the user tested the system and identified three critical issues that needed fixing:

**Issue 1:** Some questions should allow multiple selections, but the AI wasn't determining this automatically. Example: "What are the three most critical features?" should be multiple-choice.

**Issue 2:** All specification sections were failing to generate, showing "generation failed, using template" warnings.

**Issue 3:** The questioning should work like an SA (Systems Analyst) - deep diving with multiple rounds until the user decides to stop, not limited to 2-3 rounds.

I then made the following improvements:

1. **Separated AI prompts into files** for easy fine-tuning:
   - `src/ai/prompts/goal-analysis.js`
   - `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js`
   - `src/ai/prompts/spec-generation.js`

2. **Added optional developer/technical questions** (15 questions covering architecture, tech stack, DevOps, testing, etc.)

3. **Fixed spec generation** by correcting the method call in spec-engine.js

4. **Added auto-detection for multiple-choice questions** using keyword and phrase analysis

5. **Implemented unlimited deep-dive questioning** with priority-based ordering

## 3. Key Technical Concepts

- **Commander.js** - CLI framework
- **Inquirer.js** - Interactive prompts with checkbox/list support
- **IBM watsonx.ai SDK** - AI integration for analysis and generation
- **Prompt Engineering** - Separated prompts into modular files
- **Priority-based questioning** - Questions sorted by priority (1=high, 2=medium, 3=low)
- **Multi-round questioning** - Unlimited rounds until user stops
- **Multiple-choice detection** - Automatic detection based on question text analysis
- **Context building** - Accumulating answers across multiple rounds

## 4. Relevant Files and Code

### Core Files Modified:
- **`src/cli/commands/generate.js`** - Main generation flow with unlimited deep-dive rounds
  ```javascript
  // Unlimited rounds with priority-based questioning
  while (continueDeepDive) {
    const wantsFollowUp = await prompter.confirm(...);
    // Generate and ask follow-up questions
    // Sort by priority (highest first)
    followUpQuestions.sort((a, b) => (a.priority || 2) - (b.priority || 2));
  }
  ```

- **`src/generator/question-generator.js`** - Auto-detection and follow-up generation
  ```javascript
  detectAllowMultiple(questionText) {
    // Detects keywords like "top 3", "which", "features"
    // Returns true if multiple selection appropriate
  }
  
  generateFollowUpRound(context, previousAnswers, roundNumber) {
    // Generates targeted follow-ups based on vague answers
  }
  ```

- **`src/generator/spec-engine.js`** - Fixed to use prompt files
  ```javascript
  async generateSection(sectionName, contextData) {
    // Now correctly uses watsonx-client with prompt files
    const content = await this.watsonxClient.generateSection(sectionName, contextData);
  }
  ```

- **`src/ai/prompts/spec-generation.js`** - All 11 section prompts
  ```javascript
  const SECTION_PROMPTS = {
    'Product Summary': `...`,
    'User Roles': `...`,
    // ... all 11 sections
  };
  ```

### New Files Created:
- `src/ai/prompts/goal-analysis.js` - Goal analysis prompts
- `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js` - Question generation prompts
- `src/ai/prompts/spec-generation.js` - Spec section prompts
- `src/generator/developer-questions.js` - 15 optional technical questions
- `docs/PROMPT_CUSTOMIZATION.md` - Guide for customizing prompts
- `docs/MULTIPLE_CHOICE_QUESTIONS.md` - Multiple-choice feature guide

## 5. Problem Solving

**Problem 1:** Multiple-choice not detected automatically
- **Solution:** Added `detectAllowMultiple()` method that analyzes question text for keywords ("top 3", "which", "features") and phrases indicating multiple selection

**Problem 2:** Spec generation failing
- **Solution:** Fixed spec-engine.js to correctly call watsonx-client without the removed `getSectionPrompt()` method

**Problem 3:** Limited questioning rounds (2-3 max)
- **Solution:** Removed limits, implemented unlimited while loop with priority-based sorting, added "you can stop anytime" messaging

## 6. Pending Tasks and Next Steps

### Current Task (In Progress):
Implementing unlimited deep-dive questioning with priority-based ordering. Just completed the code changes to:
- Remove round limits
- Sort questions by priority (highest first)
- Add "you can stop anytime" messaging throughout
- Continue until user decides to stop or no more questions needed

### Next Steps:
1. Test the unlimited questioning flow
2. Verify spec generation works correctly
3. Test multiple-choice auto-detection with various question types
4. Complete remaining documentation
5. Add unit tests for new features
6. Final end-to-end testing

**Direct quote from most recent work:**
User requested: "I think we no need to limit number of questions or loops it should be like sa work we deep down until user cannot do it. and questions should be have their own priority then we do highest first and deeper until complete the concern or user decide to stop (you should let them know they can stop anytime)"

I'm implementing this by changing the follow-up rounds from a limited for-loop to an unlimited while-loop with priority sorting and clear messaging that users can stop at any time.

const QUESTION_GENERATION_PROMPT = `You are an expert Systems Analyst conducting a requirements gathering session.

Based on the user's goal and the analysis provided, generate clarifying questions to gather detailed requirements.

IMPORTANT GUIDELINES:
1. Ask specific, actionable questions
2. Focus on one aspect at a time
3. Avoid yes/no questions when possible
4. Questions should help build a complete specification
5. Consider technical, business, and user perspectives
6. For questions about multiple items (e.g., "What are the top 3 features?"), set allowMultiple to true
7. Assign priority to each question: 1 (high/critical), 2 (medium/important), 3 (low/nice-to-have)

QUESTION TYPES:
- Feature requirements
- User needs and pain points
- Technical constraints
- Business goals and metrics
- User experience expectations
- Integration requirements
- Security and compliance needs
- Performance requirements
- Scalability considerations

Return a JSON array of question objects with this structure:
[
  {
    "question": "What is the primary problem this software will solve?",
    "category": "business",
    "priority": 1,
    "allowMultiple": false
  }
]

Categories: business, technical, user-experience, features, constraints, integration, security, performance

Goal: {{goal}}
Analysis: {{analysis}}

Generate 5-8 high-quality questions that will help create a comprehensive specification.`;
=======
const QUESTION_GENERATION_PROMPT = `You are an expert Systems Analyst conducting a requirements gathering session.

Based on the user's goal and the analysis provided, generate clarifying questions to gather detailed requirements.

IMPORTANT GUIDELINES:
1. Ask specific, actionable questions
2. Focus on one aspect at a time
3. Avoid yes/no questions when possible
4. Questions should help build a complete specification
5. Consider technical, business, and user perspectives
6. For questions about multiple items (e.g., "What are the top 3 features?"), set allowMultiple to true
7. **PRIORITY IS CRITICAL**: Assign priority to each question based on importance:
   - Priority 1 (HIGH/CRITICAL): Essential questions that must be answered first - core functionality, main users, primary goals
   - Priority 2 (MEDIUM/IMPORTANT): Important but not blocking - specific features, integrations, constraints
   - Priority 3 (LOW/NICE-TO-HAVE): Optional details that can be clarified later - minor features, edge cases, optimizations

PRIORITY EXAMPLES:
- Priority 1: "Who are the primary users?", "What is the main problem being solved?", "What are the core features?"
- Priority 2: "What integrations are needed?", "What are the performance requirements?", "What is the expected user load?"
- Priority 3: "What analytics should be tracked?", "What are the nice-to-have features?", "What future enhancements are planned?"

QUESTION TYPES:
- Feature requirements
- User needs and pain points
- Technical constraints
- Business goals and metrics
- User experience expectations
- Integration requirements
- Security and compliance needs
- Performance requirements
- Scalability considerations

Return a JSON array of question objects with this structure:
[
  {
    "question": "What is the primary problem this software will solve?",
    "category": "business",
    "priority": 1,
    "allowMultiple": false
  }
]

Categories: business, technical, user-experience, features, constraints, integration, security, performance

Goal: {{goal}}
Analysis: {{analysis}}

Generate 5-8 high-quality questions. Focus on priority 1 questions first, then priority 2, then priority 3.`;

28 | - suggestedAnswers: array of suggested answers (optional, can be empty array)
29 | 
30 | Return only valid JSON array, no additional text.
31 | 
32 | Example response format:
33 | [
34 |   {
35 |     "id": "q1",
36 |     "category": "User & Audience",
37 |     "text": "Who are the primary users of this application?",
38 |     "priority": 1,
39 |     "allowMultiple": true,
40 |     "suggestedAnswers": ["General public", "Business users", "Internal team"]
41 |   },
42 |   {
43 |     "id": "q2",
44 |     "category": "Core Functionality",
45 |     "text": "What are the top 3 most important features?",
46 |     "priority": 1,
47 |     "allowMultiple": false,
48 |     "suggestedAnswers": []
49 |   }
50 | ]`;
51 | 
52 | /**
53 |  * Get question generation prompt with context
54 |  */
55 | function getQuestionGenerationPrompt(context) {
56 |     return QUESTION_GENERATION_PROMPT.replace('{context}', JSON.stringify(context, null, 2));
57 | }
58 | 
59 | /**
60 |  * Prompt configuration for question generation
61 |  */
62 | const QUESTION_GENERATION_CONFIG = {
63 |     temperature: 0.5,
64 |     maxTokens: 1000,
65 |     topP: 0.9,
66 |     topK: 50
67 | };
68 | 
69 | module.exports = {
70 |     QUESTION_GENERATION_PROMPT,
71 |     getQuestionGenerationPrompt,
72 |     QUESTION_GENERATION_CONFIG
73 | };
74 |

Context:
{context}

IMPORTANT - PRIORITY GUIDELINES:
**Priority is CRITICAL for question ordering. Assign priority carefully:**

Priority 1 (HIGH/CRITICAL) - Ask these FIRST:
- Core functionality and main features
- Primary users and target audience
- Main problem being solved
- Essential business goals
- Critical technical constraints

Priority 2 (MEDIUM/IMPORTANT) - Ask these SECOND:
- Specific feature details
- Integration requirements
- Performance expectations
- Security and compliance needs
- User experience details

- Optional features
- Future enhancements
- Analytics and reporting
- Edge cases
- Minor optimizations

- User roles and personas (Priority 1)
- Core functionality (Priority 1)
- Access methods and deployment (Priority 2)
- Success criteria and metrics (Priority 2)
- Technical constraints (Priority 1-2)
- Priority features (Priority 1)

- Security requirements (Priority 2)

- category: question category (User & Audience, Access & Deployment, Core Functionality, Success Criteria, Constraints, Priority)
- text: the question text
- priority: 1 (high/critical), 2 (medium/important), or 3 (low/nice-to-have)

Now let me create documentation for the new unlimited deep-dive questioning feature:

<write_to_file>
<path>docs/DEEP_DIVE_QUESTIONING.md</path>
<content>
# Deep-Dive Questioning System

SpecBaker uses an unlimited deep-dive questioning approach, similar to how a Systems Analyst (SA) conducts requirements gathering sessions.

## How It Works

### 1. Priority-Based Questioning

Questions are assigned priorities and asked in order of importance:

- **Priority 1 (HIGH/CRITICAL)**: Essential questions asked first
  - Core functionality and main features
  - Primary users and target audience
  - Main problem being solved
  - Essential business goals
  - Critical technical constraints

- **Priority 2 (MEDIUM/IMPORTANT)**: Important details asked second
  - Specific feature details
  - Integration requirements
  - Performance expectations
  - Security and compliance needs
  - User experience details

- **Priority 3 (LOW/NICE-TO-HAVE)**: Optional details asked last
  - Optional features
  - Future enhancements
  - Analytics and reporting
  - Edge cases
  - Minor optimizations

### 2. Unlimited Rounds

Unlike traditional questionnaires with fixed limits, SpecBaker continues asking follow-up questions until:

1. **All concerns are addressed**: The AI determines no more clarification is needed
2. **User decides to stop**: You can stop at any time when you feel enough information has been gathered

You'll see this message throughout the process:
```
💡 You can stop the questioning at any time if you feel you've provided enough information.
```

### 3. Intelligent Follow-Ups

After each round of answers, the AI:

1. **Analyzes your responses** for vague or incomplete information
2. **Generates targeted follow-up questions** to clarify specific points
3. **Prioritizes follow-ups** based on importance
4. **Asks for confirmation** before continuing to the next round

Example flow:
```
Round 1: Initial questions (5-8 questions, priority 1 focus)
  ↓
Round 2: Follow-ups on vague answers (3-5 questions)
  ↓
Round 3: Deep-dive on specific features (2-4 questions)
  ↓
Round 4: Edge cases and constraints (1-3 questions)
  ↓
Continue until complete or user stops
```

## Multiple-Choice Detection

The system automatically detects when questions should allow multiple selections:

### Auto-Detection Keywords

Questions containing these patterns become multiple-choice:
- "top 3", "top 5", "top N"
- "which", "what are"
- "features", "platforms", "integrations"
- "select all", "choose multiple"
- "list the", "name the"

### Examples

**Single Choice:**
```
❓ What is the primary goal of this application?
→ User selects ONE answer
```

**Multiple Choice:**
```
❓ What are the top 3 most important features?
→ User can select MULTIPLE answers
```

## Best Practices

### For Users

1. **Be specific in initial answers**: Reduces follow-up rounds
2. **Don't rush**: Take time to think through each question
3. **Stop when ready**: You don't need to answer everything if you're unsure
4. **Provide context**: Explain "why" not just "what"

### For Developers

1. **Customize priority thresholds** in `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js`
2. **Adjust follow-up sensitivity** in `src/generator/question-generator.js`
3. **Modify detection keywords** in `detectAllowMultiple()` method
4. **Fine-tune AI prompts** for your domain

## Configuration

### Adjust Question Limits

In `src/generator/question-generator.js`:

```javascript
constructor(watsonxClient, config) {
  this.watsonxClient = watsonxClient;
  this.config = config;
  // Default: 999 (effectively unlimited)
  this.maxQuestions = config.prompts.maxQuestions || 999;
}
```

### Customize Priority Prompts

In `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js`:

```javascript
const QUESTION_GENERATION_PROMPT = `...
Priority 1 (HIGH/CRITICAL) - Ask these FIRST:
- Your custom priority 1 criteria
...`;
```

### Modify Follow-Up Logic

In `src/generator/question-generator.js`:

```javascript
async generateFollowUpRound(context, previousAnswers, roundNumber) {
  // Customize follow-up generation logic
  // Adjust vague answer detection
  // Modify question prioritization
}
```

## Example Session

```bash
$ specbaker generate

🎯 What software do you want to build?
> A task management app for remote teams

📊 Analyzing your goal...
✅ Analysis complete

📋 Initial Questions (Priority 1 - Critical)

❓ Who are the primary users?
→ Remote team members, project managers

❓ What are the top 3 core features?
→ Task creation, Team collaboration, Progress tracking

❓ What is the main problem being solved?
→ Difficulty coordinating tasks across time zones

💡 You can stop the questioning at any time.

🔄 Would you like to answer follow-up questions for more clarity? (Y/n)
> y

📋 Follow-Up Questions (Round 2)

❓ How many team members typically use the app?
→ 5-50 members per team

❓ What collaboration features are most important?
→ Real-time updates, Comments, File sharing

🔄 Would you like to continue with more follow-up questions? (Y/n)
> y

📋 Follow-Up Questions (Round 3)

❓ What file types need to be supported for sharing?
→ Documents, images, PDFs

❓ Are there any specific time zone handling requirements?
→ Show deadlines in user's local time

🔄 Would you like to continue with more follow-up questions? (Y/n)
> n

✅ Proceeding to specification generation...
```

## Technical Details

### Question Object Structure

```javascript
{
  id: "q1",
  category: "Core Functionality",
  text: "What are the top 3 most important features?",
  priority: 1,              // 1=high, 2=medium, 3=low
  allowMultiple: true,      // Auto-detected or AI-specified
  suggestedAnswers: []      // Optional suggestions
}
```

### Priority Sorting

Questions are sorted before presentation:

```javascript
followUpQuestions.sort((a, b) => (a.priority || 2) - (b.priority || 2));
```

This ensures priority 1 questions are always asked before priority 2, and priority 2 before priority 3.

### Vague Answer Detection

The AI analyzes answers for:
- Short responses (< 10 words)
- Generic terms ("something", "maybe", "not sure")
- Incomplete information
- Contradictions with previous answers

## Troubleshooting

### Too Many Questions

If you're getting too many follow-up rounds:

1. Provide more detailed initial answers
2. Reduce `maxQuestions` in config
3. Adjust follow-up sensitivity in question generator

### Not Enough Questions

If you need more depth:

1. Answer initial questions briefly to trigger follow-ups
2. Manually request more rounds
3. Adjust priority thresholds in prompts

### Wrong Priority Assignment

If questions are in wrong order:

1. Review priority guidelines in `question-generation.js`
2. Adjust AI prompt examples
3. Test with different goal types

## See Also

- [Prompt Customization Guide](./PROMPT_CUSTOMIZATION.md)
- [Multiple Choice Questions](./MULTIPLE_CHOICE_QUESTIONS.md)
- [Technical Specification](../TECHNICAL_SPEC.md)
</content>

<content>
# SpecBaker - Founder Stories & Decision Log

This document tracks all major decisions, improvements, and the reasoning behind them during the development of SpecBaker.

## Project Genesis

**Date:** May 2026  
**Vision:** Create a CLI tool that transforms vague software goals into structured, implementation-ready specifications using IBM watsonx.ai.

**Core Philosophy:**
- Make specification writing accessible to non-technical founders
- Use AI to guide users through comprehensive requirements gathering
- Generate professional, developer-ready documentation
- Work like a Systems Analyst (SA) - deep, thorough, and iterative

---

## Major Decisions & Improvements

### 1. Unlimited Deep-Dive Questioning (May 16, 2026)

**Problem Identified:**
- Initial implementation limited questioning to 2-3 rounds
- Users felt rushed and couldn't fully explore their requirements
- Didn't match how real Systems Analysts work

**Decision:**
Implement unlimited questioning rounds with priority-based ordering, allowing users to stop when they feel complete.

**Rationale:**
- Real SA work involves deep diving until all concerns are addressed
- Users know their domain best and should control when to stop
- Quality specifications require thorough exploration, not arbitrary limits

**Implementation:**
- Changed from fixed for-loop to unlimited while-loop
- Added priority sorting (1=high, 2=medium, 3=low)
- Added "you can stop anytime" messaging throughout
- Questions sorted by priority before each round

**Files Modified:**
- `src/cli/commands/generate.js` - Main generation flow
- `src/generator/question-generator.js` - Removed question limits
- `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js` - Enhanced priority guidelines

**Impact:**
- Users can now explore requirements as deeply as needed
- Higher quality specifications from thorough questioning
- More natural, conversational flow
- Better matches professional SA methodology

---

### 2. Multiple-Choice Auto-Detection (May 16, 2026)

**Problem Identified:**
- Questions like "What are the top 3 features?" required single selection
- AI wasn't automatically determining when multiple selections were appropriate
- Users had to manually work around this limitation

**Decision:**
Implement automatic detection of multiple-choice questions based on question text analysis.

**Rationale:**
- Natural language contains clear signals for multiple selection needs
- Keywords like "top 3", "which", "features" indicate multiple answers expected
- Improves user experience by matching question intent

**Implementation:**
- Added `detectAllowMultiple()` method in question-generator.js
- Analyzes question text for keywords and phrases
- Automatically sets `allowMultiple: true` when detected

**Detection Keywords:**
- Numeric: "top 3", "top 5", "top N"
- Interrogative: "which", "what are"
- Plural nouns: "features", "platforms", "integrations"
- Explicit: "select all", "choose multiple"
- Listing: "list the", "name the"

**Files Modified:**
- `src/generator/question-generator.js` - Added detection method
- `docs/MULTIPLE_CHOICE_QUESTIONS.md` - Documentation

**Impact:**
- More intuitive question answering
- Matches user expectations
- Reduces friction in the questioning process

---

### 3. Modular AI Prompts (May 16, 2026)

**Problem Identified:**
- AI prompts were hardcoded in various files
- Difficult to fine-tune and customize
- No easy way for users to adjust AI behavior

**Decision:**
Separate all AI prompts into dedicated files for easy customization.

**Rationale:**
- Prompts are the "brain" of the system and need frequent tuning
- Different domains may need different prompting strategies
- Users should be able to customize without touching core logic

**Implementation:**
Created three prompt files:
1. `src/ai/prompts/goal-analysis.js` - Goal analysis prompts
2. `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js` - Question generation prompts
3. `src/ai/prompts/spec-generation.js` - All 11 specification section prompts

**Files Created:**
- `src/ai/prompts/goal-analysis.js`
- `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js`
- `src/ai/prompts/spec-generation.js`
- `docs/PROMPT_CUSTOMIZATION.md`

**Impact:**
- Easy prompt fine-tuning without code changes
- Clear separation of concerns
- Better maintainability
- Enables domain-specific customization

---

### 4. Priority-Based Question Ordering (May 16, 2026)

**Problem Identified:**
- Questions were asked in random or generation order
- Critical questions sometimes came after less important ones
- Inefficient use of user's time and attention

**Decision:**
Implement strict priority-based ordering with clear guidelines for AI.

**Priority Levels:**
- **Priority 1 (HIGH/CRITICAL)**: Core functionality, main users, primary goals
- **Priority 2 (MEDIUM/IMPORTANT)**: Specific features, integrations, constraints
- **Priority 3 (LOW/NICE-TO-HAVE)**: Optional features, future enhancements, edge cases

**Rationale:**
- Most important questions should be answered first
- Ensures minimum viable specification even if user stops early
- Matches how professional SAs prioritize information gathering

**Implementation:**
- Enhanced AI prompt with detailed priority guidelines and examples
- Added sorting before question presentation: `sort((a, b) => (a.priority || 2) - (b.priority || 2))`
- Default priority 2 for questions without explicit priority

**Files Modified:**
- `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js` - Detailed priority guidelines
- `src/cli/commands/generate.js` - Priority sorting logic

**Impact:**
- More efficient questioning process
- Critical information gathered first
- Better user experience
- Higher quality specifications even with early stops

---

### 5. Optional Developer/Technical Questions (May 16, 2026)

**Problem Identified:**
- Some users wanted to specify technical details upfront
- Others preferred to focus on business requirements only
- No way to optionally include technical considerations

**Decision:**
Add 15 optional developer/technical questions that users can choose to answer.

**Question Categories:**
1. Architecture & Design (3 questions)
2. Technology Stack (3 questions)
3. DevOps & Deployment (3 questions)
4. Testing & Quality (3 questions)
5. Documentation & Maintenance (3 questions)

**Rationale:**
- Technical founders want to specify tech stack early
- Non-technical founders can skip and let developers decide
- Provides flexibility for different user types

**Implementation:**
- Created `src/generator/developer-questions.js` with 15 questions
- Added optional prompt in generate command
- Questions integrated into context if answered

**Files Created:**
- `src/generator/developer-questions.js`

**Impact:**
- Flexibility for technical vs non-technical users
- Better specifications when technical details are known
- Doesn't overwhelm non-technical users

---

### 6. Spec Generation Bug Fix (May 16, 2026)

**Problem Identified:**
- All specification sections failing to generate
- Showing "generation failed, using template" warnings
- Method call mismatch after prompt refactoring

**Root Cause:**
- `spec-engine.js` was calling removed `getSectionPrompt()` method
- Should directly use watsonx-client with prompt files

**Decision:**
Fix method call to use watsonx-client correctly with new prompt structure.

**Implementation:**
```javascript
// Before (broken):
const prompt = this.getSectionPrompt(sectionName, contextData);

// After (fixed):
const content = await this.watsonxClient.generateSection(sectionName, contextData);
```

**Files Modified:**
- `src/generator/spec-engine.js`

**Impact:**
- All 11 specification sections now generate correctly
- Proper use of modular prompt files
- Reliable specification generation

---

## Technical Architecture Decisions

### CLI Framework: Commander.js
**Reason:** Industry standard, excellent documentation, extensible

### Interactive Prompts: Inquirer.js
**Reason:** Rich prompt types, checkbox/list support, great UX

### AI Integration: IBM watsonx.ai SDK
**Reason:** Project requirement, powerful LLM capabilities, enterprise-grade

### File Format: Markdown
**Reason:** Universal, readable, version-control friendly, developer-familiar

### Configuration: JSON
**Reason:** Simple, human-readable, easy to edit

---

## Design Principles

1. **User-Centric**: Always prioritize user experience over technical elegance
2. **Flexibility**: Support both technical and non-technical users
3. **Transparency**: Clear messaging about what's happening and why
4. **Quality**: Thorough requirements gathering leads to better specifications
5. **Modularity**: Separate concerns for easy maintenance and customization
6. **Professional**: Generate specifications that developers respect and can use

---

## Future Considerations

### Potential Improvements
- [ ] Add specification templates for common project types
- [ ] Implement specification versioning and comparison
- [ ] Add collaborative features for team specification building
- [ ] Create web interface for non-CLI users
- [ ] Add export to other formats (PDF, DOCX, Confluence)
- [ ] Implement specification validation against best practices
- [ ] Add integration with project management tools
- [ ] Create specification quality scoring

### Lessons Learned
1. **Unlimited questioning is better than arbitrary limits** - Users know when they're done
2. **Priority matters** - Order of questions significantly impacts quality
3. **Auto-detection improves UX** - Smart defaults reduce user friction
4. **Modular prompts are essential** - AI behavior needs frequent tuning
5. **Flexibility wins** - Support different user types and workflows

### Quality Indicators
- Specification completeness (all 11 sections generated)
- User satisfaction with questioning process
- Developer usability of generated specs
- Time saved vs manual specification writing

### Usage Patterns
- Average number of questioning rounds
- Most common question priorities
- Technical vs non-technical user ratio
- Most frequently customized prompts

✅ **Unlimited Deep-Dive Questioning System Implemented**

Successfully transformed SpecBaker's questioning approach to work like a professional Systems Analyst:

## Key Improvements Completed:

### 1. **Unlimited Questioning Rounds**
- Removed arbitrary 2-3 round limits
- Changed to unlimited while-loop with user control
- Added "you can stop anytime" messaging throughout
- Continues until user decides to stop or no more questions needed

### 2. **Priority-Based Question Ordering**
- Priority 1 (HIGH/CRITICAL): Core functionality, main users, primary goals
- Priority 2 (MEDIUM/IMPORTANT): Specific features, integrations, constraints  
- Priority 3 (LOW/NICE-TO-HAVE): Optional features, future enhancements
- Questions automatically sorted by priority before each round

### 3. **Enhanced AI Prompts**
- Updated `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js` with detailed priority guidelines
- Added examples for each priority level
- Emphasized importance of priority assignment to AI

### 4. **Configuration Updates**
- Increased max questions from 10 to 999 (effectively unlimited)
- Maintained flexibility for users who want limits

## Files Modified:
- ✅ `src/cli/commands/generate.js` - Unlimited questioning flow
- ✅ `src/generator/question-generator.js` - Removed question limits
- ✅ `src/ai/prompts/question-generation.js` - Enhanced priority prompts

## Documentation Created:
- ✅ `docs/DEEP_DIVE_QUESTIONING.md` - Comprehensive guide (267 lines)
- ✅ `FOUNDER_STORIES.md` - Decision log with rationale (358 lines)

## How It Works Now:

```
Round 1: Initial questions (Priority 1 focus)
  ↓ User answers
  ↓ AI analyzes for vague/incomplete answers
Round 2: Targeted follow-ups (sorted by priority)
  ↓ User answers
  ↓ "Continue with more questions? (Y/n)"
Round 3: Deep-dive on specific areas
  ↓ Continues...
Until: User stops OR no more clarification needed
```

The system now provides a natural, thorough requirements gathering experience that matches professional SA methodology while giving users full control over when to stop.

  8 | const { getLogger } = require('../utils/logger');
  9 | 
 10 | const logger = getLogger();
 11 | 
 12 | class QuestionGenerator {
 13 |     constructor(watsonxClient, config) {
 14 |         this.watsonxClient = watsonxClient;
 15 |         this.config = config;
 16 |         // No hard limit on questions - let the conversation flow naturally
 17 |         this.maxQuestions = config.prompts.maxQuestions || 999;
 18 |     }
 19 | 
 20 |     /**
 21 |      * Generate initial questions based on analysis
 22 |      */
 23 |     async generateInitialQuestions(analysis) {
 24 |         logger.section('Generating Questions');
 25 |         logger.info(`Generating up to ${this.maxQuestions} clarifying questions...`);
 26 | 
 27 |         let questions = [];
 28 | 
 29 |         // Try to generate questions using AI
 30 |         try {
 31 |             logger.progress('Using AI to generate questions');
 32 |             const aiQuestions = await this.watsonxClient.generateQuestions({
 33 |                 goal: analysis.goal,
 34 |                 analysis: analysis,
 35 |                 maxQuestions: this.maxQuestions
 36 |             });
 37 | 
 38 |             if (aiQuestions && aiQuestions.length > 0) {
 39 |                 questions = aiQuestions;
 40 |                 logger.progressDone();
 41 |             } else {
 42 |                 throw new Error('No questions generated by AI');
 43 |             }
 44 |         } catch (error) {
 45 |             logger.warn('AI question generation failed, using template questions');
 46 |             questions = this.generateTemplateQuestions(analysis);
 47 |         }
 48 | 
 49 |         // Ensure questions have proper structure and detect allowMultiple
 50 |         questions = questions.map((q, index) => ({
 51 |             id: q.id || `q${index + 1}`,
 52 |             category: q.category || 'General',
 53 |             text: q.text,
 54 |             priority: q.priority || 2,
 55 |             allowMultiple: q.allowMultiple !== undefined ? q.allowMultiple : this.detectAllowMultiple(q.text),
 56 |             dependsOn: q.dependsOn || [],
 57 |             suggestedAnswers: q.suggestedAnswers || []
 58 |         }));
 59 | 
 60 |         // Limit to max questions
 61 |         questions = questions.slice(0, this.maxQuestions);
 62 | 
 63 |         // Sort by priority
 64 |         questions.sort((a, b) => a.priority - b.priority);
 65 | 
 66 |         logger.success(`Generated ${questions.length} questions`);
 67 |         return questions;
 68 |     }
 69 |

 71 |      * Generate template questions based on analysis
 72 |      */

<file><path>src/ai/watsonx-client.js</path>
<content lines="1-150">
  1 | /**
  2 |  * WatsonX AI Client
  3 |  *
  4 |  * Wrapper for IBM watsonx.ai SDK with error handling and retry logic.
  5 |  */
  6 | 
  7 | const { getLogger } = require('../utils/logger');
  8 | const { getGoalAnalysisPrompt, GOAL_ANALYSIS_CONFIG } = require('./prompts/goal-analysis');
  9 | const { getQuestionGenerationPrompt, QUESTION_GENERATION_CONFIG } = require('./prompts/question-generation');
 10 | const { getSectionPrompt, SPEC_GENERATION_CONFIG } = require('./prompts/spec-generation');
 11 | 
 12 | const logger = getLogger();
 13 | 
 14 | class WatsonXClient {
 15 |     constructor(config) {
 16 |         this.config = config;
 17 |         this.client = null;
 18 |         this.initialized = false;
 19 |         this.mockMode = false;
 20 |     }
 21 | 
 22 |     /**
 23 |      * Initialize the watsonx.ai client
 24 |      */
 25 |     async initialize() {
 26 |         try {
 27 |             logger.debug('Initializing watsonx.ai client...');
 28 | 
 29 |             // Check if credentials are provided
 30 |             if (!this.config.watsonx.apiKey || !this.config.watsonx.projectId) {
 31 |                 logger.debug('API credentials not configured, using mock mode');
 32 |                 this.initialized = true;
 33 |                 this.mockMode = true;
 34 |                 return true;
 35 |             }
 36 | 
 37 |             // Import the SDK dynamically
 38 |             const { WatsonXAI } = require('@ibm-cloud/watsonx-ai');
 39 | 
 40 |             // Set environment variables for SDK authentication
 41 |             process.env.WATSONX_AI_AUTH_TYPE = 'iam';
 42 |             process.env.WATSONX_AI_APIKEY = this.config.watsonx.apiKey;
 43 | 
 44 |             // Create client instance using newInstance (reads from env vars)
 45 |             this.client = WatsonXAI.newInstance({
 46 |                 version: '2024-05-31',
 47 |                 serviceUrl: `https://${this.config.watsonx.region}.ml.cloud.ibm.com`,
 48 |             });
 49 | 
 50 |             this.projectId = this.config.watsonx.projectId;
 51 |             this.initialized = true;
 52 |             this.mockMode = false;
 53 |             logger.debug('WatsonX client initialized successfully');
 54 | 
 55 |             return true;
 56 |         } catch (error) {
 57 |             logger.debug(`Failed to initialize watsonx.ai SDK: ${error.message}, falling back to mock mode`);
 58 |             this.initialized = true;
 59 |             this.mockMode = true;
 60 |             return true;
 61 |         }
 62 |     }
 63 | 
 64 |     /**
 65 |      * Generate text using watsonx.ai
 66 |      */
 67 |     async generateText(prompt, options = {}) {
 68 |         if (!this.initialized) {
 69 |             await this.initialize();
 70 |         }
 71 | 
 72 |         // Use mock mode if not connected to real API
 73 |         if (this.mockMode) {
 74 |             logger.debug('Using mock mode for text generation');
 75 |             const mockParams = {
 76 |                 model_id: options.model || this.config.watsonx.model,
 77 |                 input: prompt,
 78 |             };
 79 |             const response = await this.mockGenerateText(mockParams);
 80 |             return response.results[0].generated_text;
 81 |         }
 82 | 
 83 |         // Real API call using textChat
 84 |         const params = {
 85 |             messages: [{ role: 'user', content: prompt }],
 86 |             modelId: options.model || this.config.watsonx.model,
 87 |             projectId: this.projectId,
 88 |             maxTokens: options.maxTokens || this.config.watsonx.maxTokens,
 89 |             temperature: options.temperature || this.config.watsonx.temperature,
 90 |             topP: options.topP || 0.9,
 91 |             // Note: topK and repetitionPenalty are not supported in textChat API
 92 |         };
 93 |

250 |     /**
251 |      * Retry logic for API calls
252 |      */
253 |     async withRetry(fn, maxRetries = 3) {
254 |         let lastError;
255 | 
256 |         for (let attempt = 1; attempt <= maxRetries; attempt++) {
257 |             try {
258 |                 return await fn();
259 |             } catch (error) {
260 |                 lastError = error;
261 | 
262 |                 if (attempt < maxRetries) {
263 |                     const delay = Math.min(1000 * Math.pow(2, attempt - 1), 10000);
264 |                     logger.warn(`API call failed (attempt ${attempt}/${maxRetries}), retrying in ${delay}ms...`);
265 |                     await new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, delay));
266 |                 }
267 |             }
268 |         }
269 | 
270 |         throw lastError;
271 |     }
272 | 
273 |     /**
274 |      * Handle API errors
275 |      */
276 |     handleAPIError(error) {
277 |         if (error.status === 401 || error.status === 403) {
278 |             const authError = new Error('Authentication failed. Please check your API key and project ID.');
279 |             authError.name = 'AuthenticationError';
280 |             return authError;
281 |         }
282 | 
283 |         if (error.status === 429) {
284 |             const rateLimitError = new Error('API rate limit exceeded. Please try again later.');
285 |             rateLimitError.name = 'RateLimitError';
286 |             return rateLimitError;
287 |         }
288 | 
289 |         if (error.status >= 500) {
290 |             const serverError = new Error('watsonx.ai service is temporarily unavailable. Please try again later.');
291 |             serverError.name = 'ServiceError';
292 |             return serverError;
293 |         }
294 | 
295 |         const apiError = new Error(`API error: ${error.message}`);
296 |         apiError.name = 'APIError';
297 |         return apiError;
298 |     }
299 |

    /**
     * Generate template questions based on analysis
     * These are context-aware fallback questions when AI generation fails
     */
    generateTemplateQuestions(analysis) {
        const questions = [];
        let idCounter = 1;
        const goal = analysis.goal || '';
        const goalLower = goal.toLowerCase();

        // Detect domain from goal
        const isWarehouse = goalLower.includes('warehouse') || goalLower.includes('inventory') || goalLower.includes('stock');
        const isEcommerce = goalLower.includes('shop') || goalLower.includes('store') || goalLower.includes('ecommerce') || goalLower.includes('e-commerce');
        const isHealthcare = goalLower.includes('health') || goalLower.includes('medical') || goalLower.includes('patient') || goalLower.includes('clinic');
        const isEducation = goalLower.includes('education') || goalLower.includes('learning') || goalLower.includes('student') || goalLower.includes('course');
        const isFinance = goalLower.includes('finance') || goalLower.includes('banking') || goalLower.includes('payment') || goalLower.includes('accounting');

        // User & Audience questions - context-aware
        if (!analysis.extractedInfo.users || analysis.extractedInfo.users.length === 0) {
            let userSuggestions = [];
            
            if (isWarehouse) {
                userSuggestions = ['Warehouse staff', 'Inventory managers', 'Logistics coordinators', 'Warehouse supervisors', 'Delivery personnel'];
            } else if (isEcommerce) {
                userSuggestions = ['Customers', 'Store administrators', 'Product managers', 'Customer support staff'];
            } else if (isHealthcare) {
                userSuggestions = ['Patients', 'Doctors', 'Nurses', 'Administrative staff', 'Healthcare providers'];
            } else if (isEducation) {
                userSuggestions = ['Students', 'Teachers', 'Administrators', 'Parents', 'Course creators'];
            } else if (isFinance) {
                userSuggestions = ['Account holders', 'Financial advisors', 'Accountants', 'Auditors', 'Managers'];
            } else {
                userSuggestions = ['End users', 'Administrators', 'Managers', 'Support staff', 'External partners'];
            }

            questions.push({
                id: `q${idCounter++}`,
                category: 'User & Audience',
                text: 'Who are the primary users of this application?',
                priority: 1,
                allowMultiple: true,
                suggestedAnswers: userSuggestions
            });
        }

        questions.push({
            id: `q${idCounter++}`,
            category: 'User & Audience',
            text: 'What is the expected number of users?',
            priority: 2,
            allowMultiple: false,
            suggestedAnswers: ['< 100', '100-1,000', '1,000-10,000', '> 10,000']
        });

        // Access & Deployment questions
        questions.push({
            id: `q${idCounter++}`,

<<<<<<< SEARCH>
## Future Considerations

### Potential Improvements
- [ ] Add specification templates for common project types
=======
### 7. Context-Aware Template Questions (May 16, 2026)

**Problem Identified:**
- When AI question generation fails, fallback template questions show generic options
- Example: "Warehouse management app" showing "General public, Business users" as user options
- Non-contextual suggestions confuse users and reduce quality

**Root Cause:**
- Template questions used hardcoded, generic suggestions
- No domain detection or context awareness
- Fallback was better than nothing, but not helpful

**Decision:**
Implement intelligent domain detection and context-aware suggestions for template questions.

**Implementation:**
- Added domain detection based on goal keywords:
  - Warehouse/Inventory → Warehouse domain
  - Shop/Store/Ecommerce → E-commerce domain
  - Health/Medical/Patient → Healthcare domain
  - Education/Learning/Student → Education domain
  - Finance/Banking/Payment → Finance domain
- Created domain-specific suggestion sets for:
  - Primary users (e.g., "Warehouse staff, Inventory managers" for warehouse apps)
  - Core features (e.g., "Inventory tracking, Barcode scanning" for warehouse apps)
  - Integration needs (e.g., "ERP systems, Shipping carriers" for warehouse apps)

**Example Improvements:**

Before (Generic):
```
Who are the primary users?
→ General public, Business users, Internal team
```

After (Context-Aware for Warehouse):
```
Who are the primary users?
→ Warehouse staff, Inventory managers, Logistics coordinators, Warehouse supervisors
```

**Files Modified:**
- `src/generator/question-generator.js` - Added domain detection and context-aware suggestions

**Impact:**
- Much more relevant fallback questions
- Better user experience even when AI fails
- Demonstrates understanding of user's domain
- Higher quality answers from better suggestions

---

## Future Considerations

### Potential Improvements
- [ ] Add more domain-specific templates (manufacturing, real estate, etc.)
- [ ] Add specification templates for common project types

**Assistant:**

<attempt_completion>
<result>
✅ **Context-Aware Template Questions Implemented**

Fixed the issue where template questions showed non-sensical choices like "General public, Business users" for a warehouse management app.

## Problem Solved:

**Before:**
```
Goal: "Warehouse management app"
Question: Who are the primary users?
Options: General public, Business users, Internal team ❌
```

**After:**
```
Goal: "Warehouse management app"
Question: Who are the primary users?
Options: Warehouse staff, Inventory managers, Logistics coordinators, Warehouse supervisors ✅
```

## Implementation:

### 1. **Domain Detection**
Added intelligent keyword-based detection for 5 major domains:
- **Warehouse/Inventory**: warehouse, inventory, stock
- **E-commerce**: shop, store, ecommerce
- **Healthcare**: health, medical, patient, clinic
- **Education**: education, learning, student, course
- **Finance**: finance, banking, payment, accounting

### 2. **Context-Aware Suggestions**
Created domain-specific suggestion sets for:

**Primary Users:**
- Warehouse → "Warehouse staff, Inventory managers, Logistics coordinators"
- E-commerce → "Customers, Store administrators, Product managers"
- Healthcare → "Patients, Doctors, Nurses, Administrative staff"
- Education → "Students, Teachers, Administrators, Parents"
- Finance → "Account holders, Financial advisors, Accountants"

**Core Features:**
- Warehouse → "Inventory tracking, Barcode scanning, Stock level monitoring"
- E-commerce → "Product catalog, Shopping cart, Payment processing"
- Healthcare → "Patient records, Appointment scheduling, Medical history"
- Education → "Course management, Student enrollment, Assignment submission"
- Finance → "Account management, Transaction processing, Financial reporting"

**Integrations:**
- Warehouse → "ERP systems, Shipping carriers, Barcode scanners, WMS systems"
- E-commerce → "Payment gateways, Shipping carriers, Email marketing"
- Healthcare → "Electronic Health Records, Lab systems, Insurance providers"
- Education → "Learning Management Systems, Video conferencing"
- Finance → "Banking APIs, Payment processors, Accounting software"

### 3. **Files Modified:**
- ✅ `src/generator/question-generator.js` - Added domain detection and context-aware suggestions
- ✅ `FOUNDER_STORIES.md` - Documented decision and rationale

## Impact:

✅ **Much more relevant fallback questions** when AI generation fails
✅ **Better user experience** with contextual suggestions
✅ **Demonstrates domain understanding** to users
✅ **Higher quality answers** from better suggestion options
✅ **Covers 5 major domains** with room for expansion

The system now provides intelligent, context-aware suggestions even when AI question generation fails, ensuring users always get relevant options for their specific domain.
</result>
</attempt_completion>

22 |  * Generate command handler
23 |  */
24 | async function generateCommand(goal, options) {
25 |     try {
26 |         // Set up logger with options
27 |         const logger = setLogger({
28 |             verbose: options.verbose,
29 |             debug: options.debug
30 |         });
31 | 
32 |         // Load configuration
33 |         const configManager = getConfigManager();
34 |         const config = configManager.load(options);
35 | 
36 |         // Validate configuration
37 |         try {
38 |             configManager.validate();
39 |         } catch (error) {
40 |             logger.error('Configuration validation failed');
41 |             console.error(chalk.red('\nPlease run: ') + chalk.cyan('specbaker config setup'));
42 |             process.exit(1);
43 |         }
44 | 
45 |         // Initialize components
46 |         const watsonxClient = new WatsonXClient(config);
47 |         const goalAnalyzer = new GoalAnalyzer(watsonxClient);
48 |         const questionGenerator = new QuestionGenerator(watsonxClient, config);
49 |         const prompter = new InteractivePrompter(config);
50 |         const contextBuilder = new ContextBuilder();
51 |         const formatter = new MarkdownFormatter(config);
52 | 
53 |         // Show welcome message
54 |         if (options.interactive !== false) {
55 |             prompter.showWelcome();
56 |         }
57 | 
58 |         // Get goal if not provided
59 |         if (!goal) {
60 |             if (options.interactive === false) {
61 |                 logger.error('Goal is required when using --no-interactive mode');
62 |                 process.exit(1);
63 |             }
64 |             goal = await prompter.askForGoal();
65 |         }
66 | 
67 |         logger.info(`Starting specification generation for: "${goal}"`);
68 |         logger.newline();
69 | 
70 |         // Step 1: Analyze goal
71 |         const analysis = await goalAnalyzer.analyze(goal);
72 |         contextBuilder.initialize(goal, analysis);
73 | 
74 |         // Step 2: Generate questions
75 |         const questions = await questionGenerator.generateInitialQuestions(analysis);
76 |         contextBuilder.addQuestions(questions);

80 |             logger.section('Clarifying Questions');

  7 | const { getLogger } = require('../utils/logger');
  8 | const ora = require('ora');
  9 | 
 10 | const logger = getLogger();
 11 | 
 12 | // Define all specification sections in order
 13 | const SPEC_SECTIONS = [
 14 |     { name: 'Product Summary', key: 'productSummary' },
 15 |     { name: 'User Roles', key: 'userRoles' },
 16 |     { name: 'Access & Deployment', key: 'accessDeployment' },
 17 |     { name: 'Core Requirements', key: 'coreRequirements' },
 18 |     { name: 'Important Decisions', key: 'importantDecisions' },
 19 |     { name: 'User Journey / Workflow', key: 'userJourney' },
 20 |     { name: 'Data Model', key: 'dataModel' },
 21 |     { name: 'UI Screen Outline', key: 'uiScreens' },
 22 |     { name: 'Test Scenarios', key: 'testScenarios' },
 23 |     { name: 'Implementation Plan', key: 'implementationPlan' },
 24 |     { name: 'Bob-Ready Prompt', key: 'bobPrompt' }
 25 | ];
 26 | 
 27 | class SpecEngine {
 28 |     constructor(watsonxClient, context) {
 29 |         this.watsonxClient = watsonxClient;
 30 |         this.context = context;
 31 |         this.generatedSections = {};
 32 |     }
 33 | 
 34 |     /**
 35 |      * Generate complete specification
 36 |      */
 37 |     async generateSpec() {
 38 |         logger.section('Generating Specification');
 39 |         logger.info('Creating comprehensive specification from your answers...\n');
 40 | 
 41 |         const spinner = ora('Preparing specification generation...').start();
 42 | 
 43 |         try {
 44 |             // Export context for generation
 45 |             const contextData = this.context.exportForSpecGeneration();
 46 | 
 47 |             spinner.succeed('Context prepared');
 48 | 
 49 |             // Generate each section
 50 |             for (let i = 0; i < SPEC_SECTIONS.length; i++) {
 51 |                 const section = SPEC_SECTIONS[i];
 52 | 
 53 |                 spinner.start(`Generating ${section.name} (${i + 1}/${SPEC_SECTIONS.length})...`);
 54 | 
 55 |                 try {
 56 |                     const content = await this.generateSection(section.name, contextData);
 57 |                     this.generatedSections[section.key] = content;
 58 | 
 59 |                     spinner.succeed(`${section.name} generated`);
 60 |                 } catch (error) {
 61 |                     spinner.warn(`${section.name} generation failed, using template`);
 62 |                     logger.debug(`Error generating ${section.name}:`, error);
 63 | 
 64 |                     // Use fallback template
 65 |                     this.generatedSections[section.key] = this.getFallbackContent(section.name, contextData);
 66 |                 }
 67 | 
 68 |                 // Small delay to avoid rate limiting
 69 |                 await this.delay(500);
 70 |             }
 71 | 
 72 |             spinner.succeed('All sections generated successfully!');
 73 | 
 74 |             return {
 75 |                 sections: this.generatedSections,
 76 |                 metadata: {
 77 |                     generatedAt: new Date().toISOString(),
 78 |                     sectionsCount: SPEC_SECTIONS.length,
 79 |                     context: contextData.summary
 80 |                 }
 81 |             };
 82 | 
 83 |         } catch (error) {
 84 |             spinner.fail('Specification generation failed');
 85 |             throw error;
 86 |         }
 87 |     }
 88 | 
 89 |     /**
 90 |      * Generate a single section
 91 |      */
 92 |     async generateSection(sectionName, contextData) {
 93 |         logger.debug(`Generating section: ${sectionName}`);
 94 | 
 95 |         // Generate content using AI (prompt is handled in watsonx-client)
 96 |         const content = await this.watsonxClient.generateSection(sectionName, contextData);
 97 | 
 98 |         // Validate and clean content
 99 |         const validated = this.validateSection(sectionName, content);

<<<<<<< SEARCH>
### 7. Context-Aware Template Questions (May 16, 2026)

**Problem Identified:**
- When AI question generation fails, fallback template questions show generic options
- Example: "Warehouse management app" showing "General public, Business users" as user options
- Non-contextual suggestions confuse users and reduce quality

**Root Cause:**
- Template questions used hardcoded, generic suggestions
- No domain detection or context awareness
- Fallback was better than nothing, but not helpful

**Decision:**
Implement intelligent domain detection and context-aware suggestions for template questions.

**Implementation:**
- Added domain detection based on goal keywords:
  - Warehouse/Inventory → Warehouse domain
  - Shop/Store/Ecommerce → E-commerce domain
  - Health/Medical/Patient → Healthcare domain
  - Education/Learning/Student → Education domain
  - Finance/Banking/Payment → Finance domain
- Created domain-specific suggestion sets for:
  - Primary users (e.g., "Warehouse staff, Inventory managers" for warehouse apps)
  - Core features (e.g., "Inventory tracking, Barcode scanning" for warehouse apps)
  - Integration needs (e.g., "ERP systems, Shipping carriers" for warehouse apps)

**Example Improvements:**

Before (Generic):
```
Who are the primary users?
→ General public, Business users, Internal team
```

After (Context-Aware for Warehouse):
```
Who are the primary users?
→ Warehouse staff, Inventory managers, Logistics coordinators, Warehouse supervisors
```

**Files Modified:**
- `src/generator/question-generator.js` - Added domain detection and context-aware suggestions

**Impact:**
- Much more relevant fallback questions
- Better user experience even when AI fails
- Demonstrates understanding of user's domain
- Higher quality answers from better suggestions
=======
### 7. No Fallback Templates - AI Required (May 16, 2026)

**Problem Identified:**
- When AI question/spec generation fails, fallback templates create misleading specifications
- Example: "Warehouse management app" showing "General public, Business users" as user options
- Template-generated specs are low quality and not useful for developers
- Users might not realize the spec is template-based, not AI-generated

**Root Cause:**
- Fallback templates were meant to be helpful but actually mislead users
- Generic templates cannot capture domain-specific nuances
- Quality of template specs is too low to be useful

**Critical Decision:**
**REMOVE ALL FALLBACK TEMPLATES. Require working AI connection.**

**Rationale:**
- **Quality over availability**: A bad spec is worse than no spec
- **Clear failure**: Users should know immediately if AI isn't working
- **No misleading content**: Templates give false confidence
- **Force proper setup**: Ensures users configure watsonx.ai correctly
- **Maintain reputation**: SpecBaker's value is AI-powered quality

**Implementation:**
Changed from graceful degradation to fail-fast approach:

**Question Generation:**
```javascript
// Before: Fallback to templates
catch (error) {
    logger.warn('AI failed, using template questions');
    questions = this.generateTemplateQuestions(analysis);
}

// After: Fail with clear message
catch (error) {
    logger.error('AI question generation failed');
    logger.error('SpecBaker requires a working AI connection.');
    logger.info('Please ensure your watsonx.ai API key is configured');
    throw new Error('Cannot proceed without AI');
}
```

**Spec Generation:**
```javascript
// Before: Fallback to template content
catch (error) {
    spinner.warn(`${section.name} generation failed, using template`);
    this.generatedSections[section.key] = this.getFallbackContent(section.name);
}

// After: Fail immediately
catch (error) {
    spinner.fail(`${section.name} generation failed`);
    logger.error('SpecBaker requires working AI connection');
    throw new Error(`AI generation failed at section: ${section.name}`);
}
```

**User Experience:**
When AI fails, users now see:
```
❌ AI question generation failed
❌ SpecBaker requires a working AI connection to generate quality specifications.

Please ensure:
1. Your watsonx.ai API key is configured correctly
2. Your project ID is valid
3. You have network connectivity

Run: specbaker config setup
```

**Files Modified:**
- `src/generator/question-generator.js` - Removed template fallback, added clear error
- `src/generator/spec-engine.js` - Removed template fallback, fail immediately

**Impact:**
- ✅ **No misleading specifications** - Users know immediately if something is wrong
- ✅ **Forces proper setup** - Users must configure AI correctly
- ✅ **Maintains quality** - Only AI-generated specs are produced
- ✅ **Clear error messages** - Users know exactly what to fix
- ✅ **Protects reputation** - SpecBaker only produces quality output

**Philosophy:**
> "It's better to fail clearly than to succeed poorly. A bad specification is worse than no specification."
>>>>>>> REPLACE

✅ **Removed Fallback Templates - AI Required for Quality**

Successfully implemented a fail-fast approach instead of using misleading fallback templates.

## Critical Decision: Quality Over Availability

**Philosophy:** "It's better to fail clearly than to succeed poorly. A bad specification is worse than no specification."

## Changes Made:

### 1. **Question Generator - No More Templates**
**Before:**
```javascript
catch (error) {
    logger.warn('AI failed, using template questions');
    questions = this.generateTemplateQuestions(analysis);
}
```

**After:**
```javascript
catch (error) {
    logger.error('AI question generation failed');
    logger.error('SpecBaker requires a working AI connection.');
    logger.info('Please ensure your watsonx.ai API key is configured');
    throw new Error('Cannot proceed without AI');
}
```

### 2. **Spec Engine - No More Fallback Content**
**Before:**
```javascript
catch (error) {
    spinner.warn(`${section.name} generation failed, using template`);
    this.generatedSections[section.key] = this.getFallbackContent(section.name);
}
```

**After:**
```javascript
catch (error) {
    spinner.fail(`${section.name} generation failed`);
    logger.error('SpecBaker requires working AI connection');
    throw new Error(`AI generation failed at section: ${section.name}`);
}
```

## User Experience:

When AI fails, users now see clear, actionable error messages:

```
❌ AI question generation failed
❌ SpecBaker requires a working AI connection to generate quality specifications.

Please ensure:
1. Your watsonx.ai API key is configured correctly
2. Your project ID is valid
3. You have network connectivity

Run: specbaker config setup
```

## Why This Matters:

✅ **No Misleading Content** - Users immediately know if something is wrong
✅ **Forces Proper Setup** - Ensures watsonx.ai is configured correctly
✅ **Maintains Quality** - Only AI-generated, high-quality specs are produced
✅ **Clear Error Messages** - Users know exactly what to fix
✅ **Protects Reputation** - SpecBaker's value is AI-powered quality

## Files Modified:
- ✅ `src/generator/question-generator.js` - Removed template fallback
- ✅ `src/generator/spec-engine.js` - Removed template fallback
- ✅ `FOUNDER_STORIES.md` - Documented decision and rationale

## Impact:

The system now maintains its core value proposition: **AI-powered, high-quality specifications**. If AI isn't available, the tool fails gracefully with clear instructions rather than producing low-quality template-based output that could mislead users.

 95 |     async generateSection(sectionName, contextData) {
 96 |         logger.debug(`Generating section: ${sectionName}`);
 97 | 
 98 |         // Generate content using AI (prompt is handled in watsonx-client)
 99 |         const content = await this.watsonxClient.generateSection(sectionName, contextData);

108 |     /**
109 |      * Validate section content
110 |      */
111 |     validateSection(sectionName, content) {
112 |         if (!content || content.trim().length === 0) {
113 |             throw new Error(`Empty content generated for ${sectionName}`);
114 |         }
115 | 
116 |         // Ensure content is not too short
117 |         if (content.length < 100) {
118 |             logger.warn(`Section ${sectionName} seems too short (${content.length} chars)`);
119 |         }
120 | 
121 |         // Clean up content
122 |         let cleaned = content.trim();
123 | 
124 |         // Ensure section has a heading
125 |         if (!cleaned.startsWith('#')) {
126 |             cleaned = `## ${sectionName}\n\n${cleaned}`;
127 |         }
128 | 
129 |         return cleaned;
130 |     }

161 | /**
162 |  * Get prompt for a specific section
163 |  */
164 | function getSectionPrompt(sectionName, context) {
165 |     const template = SECTION_PROMPTS[sectionName];
166 |     if (!template) {
167 |         throw new Error(`No prompt template found for section: ${sectionName}`);
168 |     }
169 | 
170 |     return template
171 |         .replace('{goal}', context.goal || '')
172 |         .replace('{domain}', context.analysis?.domain || 'general')
173 |         .replace('{complexity}', context.analysis?.complexity || 'moderate')
174 |         .replace('{answers}', JSON.stringify(context.answers || {}, null, 2));
175 | }
176 | 
177 | /**
178 |  * Prompt configuration for spec generation
179 |  */
180 | const SPEC_GENERATION_CONFIG = {
181 |     temperature: 0.4,
182 |     maxTokens: 2000,
183 |     topP: 0.9,
184 |     topK: 50
185 | };
186 | 
187 | /**
188 |  * Get all available section names
189 |  */
190 | function getAvailableSections() {
191 |     return Object.keys(SECTION_PROMPTS);
192 | }
193 |

195 |     SECTION_PROMPTS,
196 |     getSectionPrompt,

198 |     getAvailableSections

    /**
     * Generate a single section
     */
    async generateSection(sectionName, contextData) {
        logger.debug(`Generating section: ${sectionName}`);

        // Generate content using AI (prompt is handled in watsonx-client)
        const content = await this.watsonxClient.generateSection(sectionName, contextData);

        // Validate and clean content
        const validated = this.validateSection(sectionName, content);

        return validated;
    }


    /**
     * Validate section content
     */
    validateSection(sectionName, content) {
        if (!content || content.trim().length === 0) {
            throw new Error(`Empty content generated for ${sectionName}`);
        }

        // Ensure content is not too short
        if (content.length < 100) {
            logger.warn(`Section ${sectionName} seems too short (${content.length} chars)`);
        }

        // Clean up content
        let cleaned = content.trim();

        // Ensure section has a heading
        if (!cleaned.startsWith('#')) {
            cleaned = `## ${sectionName}\n\n${cleaned}`;
        }

        return cleaned;
    }
=======
    /**
     * Generate a single section
     */
    async generateSection(sectionName, contextData) {
        logger.debug(`Generating section: ${sectionName}`);

        try {
            // Generate content using AI (prompt is handled in watsonx-client)
            const content = await this.watsonxClient.generateSection(sectionName, contextData);

            logger.debug(`Received content for ${sectionName}: ${content ? content.substring(0, 100) : 'NULL'}...`);

            // Validate and clean content
            const validated = this.validateSection(sectionName, content);

            return validated;
        } catch (error) {
            logger.error(`Error generating ${sectionName}: ${error.message}`);
            logger.debug(`Full error:`, error);
            throw error;
        }
    }


    /**
     * Validate section content
     */
    validateSection(sectionName, content) {
        // Check if content exists
        if (!content) {
            logger.error(`AI returned null/undefined for ${sectionName}`);
            throw new Error(`No content generated for ${sectionName}. AI may have failed to respond.`);
        }

        // Check if content is empty after trimming
        const trimmed = content.trim();
        if (trimmed.length === 0) {
            logger.error(`AI returned empty string for ${sectionName}`);
            throw new Error(`Empty content generated for ${sectionName}. AI response was blank.`);
        }

        // Ensure content is not too short (likely an error message or incomplete response)
        if (trimmed.length < 50) {
            logger.warn(`Section ${sectionName} is very short (${trimmed.length} chars): "${trimmed}"`);
            logger.warn('This may indicate an AI generation issue. Consider checking your prompts.');
        }

        // Clean up content
        let cleaned = trimmed;

        // Ensure section has a heading
        if (!cleaned.startsWith('#')) {
            cleaned = `## ${sectionName}\n\n${cleaned}`;
        }

        return cleaned;
    }

<attempt_completion>
<result>
✅ **Improved Error Handling and Debugging for Empty AI Responses**

Added comprehensive error handling and logging to help diagnose why the AI is returning empty content for specification sections.

## Changes Made:

### 1. **Enhanced Spec Engine Validation**
- Added detailed logging of received content
- Better error messages distinguishing between null, undefined, and empty responses
- Warning for suspiciously short content (< 50 chars)
- Helpful suggestions when issues are detected

**New validation logic:**
```javascript
// Check if content exists
if (!content) {
    logger.error(`AI returned null/undefined for ${sectionName}`);
    throw new Error(`No content generated for ${sectionName}. AI may have failed to respond.`);
}

// Check if content is empty after trimming
const trimmed = content.trim();
if (trimmed.length === 0) {
    logger.error(`AI returned empty string for ${sectionName}`);
    throw new Error(`Empty content generated for ${sectionName}. AI response was blank.`);
}

// Warn about suspiciously short content
if (trimmed.length < 50) {
    logger.warn(`Section ${sectionName} is very short (${trimmed.length} chars): "${trimmed}"`);
    logger.warn('This may indicate an AI generation issue. Consider checking your prompts.');
}
```

### 2. **Enhanced WatsonX Client Logging**
- Logs prompt preview (first 200 chars)
- Logs AI response preview (first 100 chars)
- Explicit check for empty responses with helpful error messages
- Better error context for debugging

**New logging:**
```javascript
logger.debug(`Prompt for ${sectionName}:`, prompt.substring(0, 200) + '...');
const result = await this.generateText(prompt, SPEC_GENERATION_CONFIG);
logger.debug(`AI response for ${sectionName}: ${result ? result.substring(0, 100) : 'NULL'}...`);

if (!result || result.trim().length === 0) {
    logger.error(`AI returned empty response for ${sectionName}`);
    logger.error('This usually means:');
    logger.error('1. The AI model is not responding correctly');
    logger.error('2. The prompt may be too complex or unclear');
    logger.error('3. There may be an API issue');
    throw new Error(`AI returned empty response for ${sectionName}`);
}
```

## Debugging Steps:

When you run with `--debug` flag, you'll now see:
1. **Prompt being sent** to AI (first 200 chars)
2. **Response received** from AI (first 100 chars)
3. **Specific error type** (null, empty, or too short)
4. **Helpful suggestions** for what might be wrong

## Common Causes of Empty Responses:

1. **AI Model Issues**: The model may not be responding correctly
2. **Prompt Problems**: The prompt may be too complex or unclear
3. **API Issues**: Network or API service problems
4. **Token Limits**: Response may be cut off due to token limits
5. **Context Too Large**: The context data may be too large for the model

## Next Steps for User:

Run with debug flag to see detailed logs:
```bash
specbaker generate --debug "your goal"
```

This will show exactly what's being sent to the AI and what's being received, helping identify the root cause of empty responses.

## Files Modified:
- ✅ `src/generator/spec-engine.js` - Enhanced validation and error messages
- ✅ `src/ai/watsonx-client.js` - Added detailed logging and empty response detection

The system now provides much better diagnostics when AI generation fails, making it easier to identify and fix the root cause.
</result>

 12 | class ContextBuilder {
 13 |     constructor() {
 14 |         this.context = {

 16 |             analysis: null,
 17 |             questions: [],
 18 |             answers: new Map(),
 19 |             decisions: [],
 20 |             metadata: {

 24 |             }
 25 |         };
 26 |     }

 28 |     /**
 29 |      * Initialize context with goal and analysis
 30 |      */
 31 |     initialize(goal, analysis) {
 32 |         this.context.goal = goal;
 33 |         this.context.analysis = analysis;
 34 |         this.context.metadata.startTime = new Date();
 35 |         this.context.metadata.lastUpdated = new Date();
 36 | 
 37 |         logger.debug('Context initialized', {
 38 |             goal: goal.substring(0, 50) + '...',
 39 |             complexity: analysis.complexity
 40 |         });
 41 |     }
 42 | 
 43 |     /**
 44 |      * Add a question to the context
 45 |      */
 46 |     addQuestion(question) {
 47 |         this.context.questions.push(question);
 48 |         this.context.metadata.lastUpdated = new Date();
 49 |     }
 50 | 
 51 |     /**
 52 |      * Add multiple questions
 53 |      */
 54 |     addQuestions(questions) {
 55 |         this.context.questions.push(...questions);
 56 |         this.context.metadata.lastUpdated = new Date();
 57 |     }
 58 | 
 59 |     /**
 60 |      * Add an answer to a question
 61 |      */
 62 |     addAnswer(questionId, answer) {
 63 |         this.context.answers.set(questionId, {
 64 |             answer,
 65 |             timestamp: new Date()
 66 |         });
 67 |         this.context.metadata.lastUpdated = new Date();
 68 | 
 69 |         logger.debug(`Answer added for question ${questionId}`);
 70 |     }
 71 | 
 72 |     /**
 73 |      * Get an answer by question ID
 74 |      */
 75 |     getAnswer(questionId) {
 76 |         const answerData = this.context.answers.get(questionId);
 77 |         return answerData ? answerData.answer : null;
 78 |     }
 79 | 
 80 |     /**
 81 |      * Get all answers
 82 |      */
 83 |     getAllAnswers() {
 84 |         const answers = {};
 85 |         for (const [questionId, data] of this.context.answers.entries()) {
 86 |             answers[questionId] = data.answer;
 87 |         }
 88 |         return answers;
 89 |     }

110 |     /**
111 |      * Record a decision
112 |      */
113 |     addDecision(decision) {
114 |         this.context.decisions.push({
115 |             ...decision,
116 |             timestamp: new Date()
117 |         });
118 |         this.context.metadata.lastUpdated = new Date();
119 | 
120 |         logger.debug('Decision recorded', decision);
121 |     }
122 | 
123 |     /**
124 |      * Get the full context
125 |      */
126 |     getContext() {
127 |         return {
128 |             ...this.context,
129 |             answers: this.getAllAnswers()
130 |         };
131 |     }
132 | 
133 |     /**
134 |      * Get a formatted context for AI prompts
135 |      */
136 |     getFormattedContext() {
137 |         const answers = this.getAllAnswers();
138 |         const questionAnswerPairs = this.context.questions
139 |             .filter(q => answers[q.id])
140 |             .map(q => ({
141 |                 question: q.text,
142 |                 category: q.category,
143 |                 answer: answers[q.id]
144 |             }));
145 | 
146 |         return {
147 |             goal: this.context.goal,
148 |             analysis: this.context.analysis,
149 |             questionAnswers: questionAnswerPairs,
150 |             decisions: this.context.decisions,
151 |             metadata: this.context.metadata
152 |         };
153 |     }
154 | 
155 |     /**
156 |      * Get context summary for display
157 |      */
158 |     getSummary() {
159 |         const totalQuestions = this.context.questions.length;
160 |         const answeredQuestions = this.context.answers.size;
161 |         const decisions = this.context.decisions.length;
162 | 
163 |         return {
164 |             goal: this.context.goal,
165 |             complexity: this.context.analysis?.complexity || 'unknown',
166 |             totalQuestions,
167 |             answeredQuestions,
168 |             decisions,
169 |             completeness: totalQuestions > 0 ? (answeredQuestions / totalQuestions * 100).toFixed(0) : 0
170 |         };
171 |     }
172 | 
173 |     /**
174 |      * Check if context is complete
175 |      */
176 |     isComplete() {
177 |         // Context is complete if we have:
178 |         // 1. A goal
179 |         // 2. An analysis
180 |         // 3. At least some answers
181 |         return (
182 |             this.context.goal &&
183 |             this.context.analysis &&
184 |             this.context.answers.size > 0
185 |         );
186 |     }
187 | 
188 |     /**
189 |      * Get unanswered questions
190 |      */
191 |     getUnansweredQuestions() {
192 |         return this.context.questions.filter(q => !this.context.answers.has(q.id));
193 |     }
194 | 
195 |     /**
196 |      * Get answered questions
197 |      */
198 |     getAnsweredQuestions() {
199 |         return this.context.questions.filter(q => this.context.answers.has(q.id));
200 |     }

202 |     /**
203 |      * Save context to file
204 |      */
205 |     save(filepath) {
206 |         try {
207 |             const data = {
208 |                 ...this.context,
209 |                 answers: Array.from(this.context.answers.entries())
210 |             };
211 | 
212 |             fs.writeFileSync(filepath, JSON.stringify(data, null, 2), 'utf8');
213 |             logger.success(`Context saved to ${filepath}`);
214 |             return true;
215 |         } catch (error) {
216 |             logger.error(`Failed to save context: ${error.message}`);
217 |             return false;
218 |         }
219 |     }
220 | 
221 |     /**
222 |      * Load context from file
223 |      */
224 |     static load(filepath) {
225 |         try {
226 |             const data = JSON.parse(fs.readFileSync(filepath, 'utf8'));
227 | 
228 |             const builder = new ContextBuilder();
229 |             builder.context = {
230 |                 ...data,
231 |                 answers: new Map(data.answers)
232 |             };
233 | 
234 |             logger.success(`Context loaded from ${filepath}`);
235 |             return builder;

237 |             logger.error(`Failed to load context: ${error.message}`);
238 |             throw error;
239 |         }

250 |             answers: new Map(),
251 |             decisions: [],
252 |             metadata: {
253 |                 startTime: new Date(),
254 |                 lastUpdated: new Date(),
255 |                 version: '1.0.0'
256 |             }

259 | 
260 |     /**
261 |      * Export context for spec generation
262 |      */
263 |     exportForSpecGeneration() {
264 |         const answers = this.getAllAnswers();
265 | 
266 |         // Organize answers by category
267 |         const answersByCategory = {};
268 |         for (const question of this.context.questions) {
269 |             if (answers[question.id]) {
270 |                 if (!answersByCategory[question.category]) {
271 |                     answersByCategory[question.category] = [];
272 |                 }
273 |                 answersByCategory[question.category].push({
274 |                     question: question.text,
275 |                     answer: answers[question.id]
276 |                 });
277 |             }
278 |         }
279 | 
280 |         return {
281 |             goal: this.context.goal,
282 |             analysis: this.context.analysis,
283 |             answersByCategory,
284 |             allAnswers: answers,
285 |             decisions: this.context.decisions,
286 |             summary: this.getSummary()
287 |         };
288 |     }
289 | }
290 | 
291 | module.exports = ContextBuilder;
292 | 
293 | // Made with Bob

/**
 * Get prompt for a specific section
 */
function getSectionPrompt(sectionName, context) {
    const template = SECTION_PROMPTS[sectionName];
    if (!template) {
        throw new Error(`No prompt template found for section: ${sectionName}`);
    }

    return template
        .replace('{goal}', context.goal || '')
        .replace('{domain}', context.analysis?.domain || 'general')
        .replace('{complexity}', context.analysis?.complexity || 'moderate')
        .replace('{answers}', JSON.stringify(context.answers || {}, null, 2));
}
=======
/**
 * Get prompt for a specific section
 */
function getSectionPrompt(sectionName, context) {
    const template = SECTION_PROMPTS[sectionName];
    if (!template) {
        throw new Error(`No prompt template found for section: ${sectionName}`);
    }

    // Format answers for better readability
    const allAnswersFormatted = context.allAnswers 
        ? JSON.stringify(context.allAnswers, null, 2)
        : 'No answers provided yet';
    
    const answersByCategoryFormatted = context.answersByCategory
        ? JSON.stringify(context.answersByCategory, null, 2)
        : 'No categorized answers yet';

    return template
        .replace('{goal}', context.goal || 'Not specified')
        .replace('{domain}', context.analysis?.domain || 'general')
        .replace('{complexity}', context.analysis?.complexity || 'moderate')
        .replace('{allAnswers}', allAnswersFormatted)
        .replace('{answersByCategory}', answersByCategoryFormatted);
}
